The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\\n39: //!   \\\"backtrace\\\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n39: //!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\n43: //!\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\n46: //!\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n51: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs%3FL1-50"}}}

structure and selection algorithm. Here's how trait obligations are resolved:\\n\\n## 1. ObligationForest - Core Data Structure\\nThe foundation of the trait obligation system is the `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs). This utility data structure tracks outstanding trait obligations that haven't yet been resolved. Obligations form a tree structure where each obligation can have sub-obligations. The forest processes obligations and returns outcomes with completed obligations and errors.\\n\\nThe `ObligationForest` uses a generic `ForestObligation` trait to allow different obligation types. `PendingPredicateObligation` is the concrete implementation used in trait selection, defined in compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs.\\n\\n## 2. FulfillmentContext - Orchestrating Obligation Resolution\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) drives the trait resolution process. It wraps an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation>` and provides methods to:\\n- Register new root obligations\\n- Process obligations through the forest\\n- Return fulfillment errors for unsatisfied obligations\\n\\nDuring the fulfillment process, the `FulfillProcessor` (a struct implementing `ObligationProcessor`) works with a `SelectionContext` to process each obligation.\\n\\n## 3. Trait Selection - SelectionContext\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is responsible for determining whether a trait obligation can be satisfied. It orchestrates the entire selection process with the following steps:\\n\\n### 3a. Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)\\nThe `assemble_candidates` method collects all possible candidates that could satisfy a trait obligation:\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_impls` - searches for matching trait impls in the codebase\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds` - checks where-clause bounds\\n- `assemble_builtin_copy_clone_candidate` - for builtin traits like Copy and Clone\\n- Other specialized candidate assembly methods for specific lang items\\n\\n### 3b. Impl Matching (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs)\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars` struct implements matching logic that tests whether an impl header can be unified with the obligation. Matching involves:\\n- Replacing bound regions in the obligation with placeholders\\n- Unifying the impl header with the obligation\\n- Checking for placeholder leaks (where placeholders relate to non-impl regions)\\n\\n### 3c. Candidate Confirmation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs)\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate` confirms it and returns:\\n- The impl source (UserDefined, Builtin, etc.)\\n- Any nested obligations required by the impl\\n\\n## 4. Error Reporting - Unsatisfied Trait Bounds\\nWhen trait obligations cannot be satisfied, error reporting occurs through:\\n\\n### 4a. Error Types (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/mod.rs)\\n`FulfillmentError` combines:\\n- The obligation that failed\\n- `FulfillmentErrorCode` which can be:\\n  - `Select(SelectionError)` - trait selection failed (Unimplemented is primary error)\\n  - `Project(MismatchedProjectionTypes)` - associated type mismatch\\n  - `Ambiguity` - multiple possible solutions\\n\\n### 4b. Error Reporting Pipeline (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs)\\nThe `report_selection_error` method handles different error scenarios:\\n- For `SelectionError::Unimplemented` - trait not implemented for the type\\n- Provides specific context from well-formedness checking\\n- Generates helpful suggestions for common mistakes\\n\\n### 4c. Main Error Reporter (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs)\\nThe `report_fulfillment_errors` method in `TypeErrCtxt` is the entry point for reporting all trait bound errors. It processes multiple errors and coordinates with suggestion providers to give users helpful guidance.\\n\\n## End-to-End Flow\\n1. Obligations are registered in `FulfillmentContext`\\n2. `process_obligations` is called on the `ObligationForest`\\n3. `FulfillProcessor` works with `SelectionContext` for each obligation\\n4. `assemble_candidates` collects all possible trait impl matches\\n5. `MatchAgainstFreshVars` determines if impls match the obligation\\n6. Successful matches are confirmed, returning nested obligations\\n7. Unfulfillable obligations become errors\\n8. `report_fulfillment_errors` generates user-facing error messages with suggestions\\n\\nThis architecture ensures efficient trait obligation resolution while providing detailed error messages when traits cannot be satisfied.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":10101,"cache_read_input_tokens":84436,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":10101},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5ea87834-8172-4e25-b3dc-f5803aac9265","uuid":"2a02169d-40c7-412f-9cd9-292f4d530e0a"}

Here's how trait obligations are resolved:\\n\\n## 1. ObligationForest - Core Data Structure\\nThe foundation of the trait obligation system is the `ObligationForest` (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs). This utility data structure tracks outstanding trait obligations that haven't yet been resolved. Obligations form a tree structure where each obligation can have sub-obligations. The forest processes obligations and returns outcomes with completed obligations and errors.\\n\\nThe `ObligationForest` uses a generic `ForestObligation` trait to allow different obligation types. `PendingPredicateObligation` is the concrete implementation used in trait selection, defined in compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs.\\n\\n## 2. FulfillmentContext - Orchestrating Obligation Resolution\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs) drives the trait resolution process. It wraps an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation>` and provides methods to:\\n- Register new root obligations\\n- Process obligations through the forest\\n- Return fulfillment errors for unsatisfied obligations\\n\\nDuring the fulfillment process, the `FulfillProcessor` (a struct implementing `ObligationProcessor`) works with a `SelectionContext` to process each obligation.\\n\\n## 3. Trait Selection - SelectionContext\\nThe `SelectionContext` (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs) is responsible for determining whether a trait obligation can be satisfied. It orchestrates the entire selection process with the following steps:\\n\\n### 3a. Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)\\nThe `assemble_candidates` method collects all possible candidates that could satisfy a trait obligation:\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_impls` - searches for matching trait impls in the codebase\\n- `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds` - checks where-clause bounds\\n- `assemble_builtin_copy_clone_candidate` - for builtin traits like Copy and Clone\\n- Other specialized candidate assembly methods for specific lang items\\n\\n### 3b. Impl Matching (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs)\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars` struct implements matching logic that tests whether an impl header can be unified with the obligation. Matching involves:\\n- Replacing bound regions in the obligation with placeholders\\n- Unifying the impl header with the obligation\\n- Checking for placeholder leaks (where placeholders relate to non-impl regions)\\n\\n### 3c. Candidate Confirmation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs)\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate` confirms it and returns:\\n- The impl source (UserDefined, Builtin, etc.)\\n- Any nested obligations required by the impl\\n\\n## 4. Error Reporting - Unsatisfied Trait Bounds\\nWhen trait obligations cannot be satisfied, error reporting occurs through:\\n\\n### 4a. Error Types (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/mod.rs)\\n`FulfillmentError` combines:\\n- The obligation that failed\\n- `FulfillmentErrorCode` which can be:\\n  - `Select(SelectionError)` - trait selection failed (Unimplemented is primary error)\\n  - `Project(MismatchedProjectionTypes)` - associated type mismatch\\n  - `Ambiguity` - multiple possible solutions\\n\\n### 4b. Error Reporting Pipeline (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs)\\nThe `report_selection_error` method handles different error scenarios:\\n- For `SelectionError::Unimplemented` - trait not implemented for the type\\n- Provides specific context from well-formedness checking\\n- Generates helpful suggestions for common mistakes\\n\\n### 4c. Main Error Reporter (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs)\\nThe `report_fulfillment_errors` method in `TypeErrCtxt` is the entry point for reporting all trait bound errors. It processes multiple errors and coordinates with suggestion providers to give users helpful guidance.\\n\\n## End-to-End Flow\\n1. Obligations are registered in `FulfillmentContext`\\n2. `process_obligations` is called on the `ObligationForest`\\n3. `FulfillProcessor` works with `SelectionContext` for each obligation\\n4. `assemble_candidates` collects all possible trait impl matches\\n5. `MatchAgainstFreshVars` determines if impls match the obligation\\n6. Successful matches are confirmed, returning nested obligations\\n7. Unfulfillable obligations become errors\\n8. `report_fulfillment_errors` generates user-facing error messages with suggestions\\n\\nThis architecture ensures efficient trait obligation resolution while providing detailed error messages when traits cannot be satisfied.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
